  14. I bought this to replace my Panasonic inductive charging shaver, whose batteries had finally died. They were replaceable, but by the time you add up the cost of the replacement batteries, a foil assembly, and the cutter, you might as well buy a new shaver. And anyway, technology marches on, so you may discover that the newest models are still better than your rebuilt one anyway. <br /> <br />And that's the case with this \\"linear motor\\" Vortex shaver. When I opened the box, I almost sent it right back because it did NOT have the inductive charging system (online sources listed it as a model that did), and the shaver felt light and flimsy. But the Amazon price was so good that I decided to give it a try, and the power cord plugs into the base with the same jack as on the razor, so you can take just the cord and shaver on a trip and dispense with the huge base, if you like. And I do like, because I typically shave dry while I'm deciding what to wear in the morning, so I don't use the base often anyway. <br /> <br />I have a heavy, stiff Scottish beard, and most electrics leave a lot of stubble, especially on my neck. But this one hacks it all down in fine style. My \\"new\\" 5-O'clock shadow is about the same as my \\"old\\" 2-O'clock shadow. Also, the small pop-up trimmer is precise enough to permit trimming around your ears and other areas in between haircuts (yes, I'm also cheap). Battery life is a tad shorter than with my old Panasonic, but then this one has that 13,000 RPM Linear motor, and extra LEDs to power. But it still lasts more than a week, and part of the reason for the shorter life may be related to the fact that now I shave a bit longer because this model gets my face almost blade-close with a dry shave. So I tend to see if I can get every last whisker. <br /> <br />I have yet to be cut or nicked with this razor, even though I have to shave inside the corners of my mouth every 2 or 3 days (picture, if you will, the caveman in the Geico commercials). Also, the pivot mechanism, which can be locked, combined with that middle slotted blade, helps get every last whisker, even those quarter-inch long \\"rogue's\\" that sometimes magically appear on a man's upper cheek, or neck. <br /> <br />The linear motor in this shaver will maintain its 13,000 RPM speed through heavy beard growth right up to the moment the batteries die. But this unit has a series of LEDs to tell you when the charge is low, so if you get caught, it's your own fault. <br /> <br />One last plus: The on-off switch is recessed, so the probability that this shaver will get switched on in your luggage is very low, of not zero. My old shaver had a slider switch, and that was a problem. <br /> <br />PS: The charger base has an annoying, huge, blinking red light, so you may have to place the base somewhere other than your nightstand.

  40. The Panasonic ES8077S is a mid-range shaver in the Panasonic line-up of electric shavers. For the price, it does the job very well, so unless you have money to burn, there is no need to buy higher-end models costing several hundred dollars. I bought this shaver because I was tired of the day-after skin irritation that occurred after I shaved with a razor. The ES8077S features three cutting blades, a sideburn trimmer and a powerful 13,000 RPM motor. The blade head can move side-to-side, but I prefer to lock it in position. The best features of this shaver are: 1) It shaves very close and relatively irritation free. You will need to do a slight touch-up with a razor afterwards in hard-to-reach areas like portions of the neck and a little of the lip area right under your nose, but this is the case with all electric shavers; 2) The rechargeable battery lasts for four shaves with 3-day stubble; quite good in my opinion; 3) The shaver can be used in the shower, and with warm water and a light layer of shaving cream applied to the skin. Braun shavers can't be used in the shower. I find that the ES8077S actually shaves better and more comfortably wet than dry; 4) Cleaning the blades and foil is easy -- just apply liquid handsoap to the foil and run the shaver under running warm water, then remove the foil and rinse it out, as well as the blades; 5) It comes with a cleaning, drying and charging station. The cleaning feature uses cartridges and is really unnecessary, since it is so easy to clean the shaver using warm water and soap, but the station will blow-dry and heat your shaver dry, as well as charge it. The blades will last 2 years; the foil 1 year, according to the manual. Overall, I'm very pleased with this shaver.

In contrast, this new pansonic vortex seems to be an improvement over even my older panasonic in that it has a triple blade system. The old panasonic and brauns have two blades on either side of a central comb that i suppose guides and preps the hair. on the vortex, that center comb also has a blade to cut long/stray hairs, and so far doesn't seem to be just a gimmick, i feel a difference. furthermore, the panasonic is a wet/dry system while braun is strictly dry. i use panasonic only dry and am already satisfied, but the unit is supposed to be watertight and panasonic invites you to try using the shaver with shaving foam for an even closer shave, not even an option with the braun. dry panasonic shave for me is already closer and faster than dry braun, nice to know if need be for special occasion, important interview or date, can try using the panasonic wet for supposedly aneven closer shave. the panasonics do a better job of hugging the contours of your face than the brauns as the head pivots in more directions. quieter motor, higher frequency hum than braun, which has a loud and harsh noise that had not improved at all with the new Activator. they are also lighter units than brauns, which i happen to like. handle is also more contoured for gripping too, braun is just a brick shape. some might say the panasonic feels cheaper/more flimsy, but i feel that the shave outcome is more important. braun has fancier packaging, the unit, the plug, the carrying case, manual, even the box (as i recall was a doozy to open). the panasonic is no nonsense but gets the job done. the panasonic cleaning unit itself has a little larger footprint than the braun; though may be easier to pack as it can lie flat and is thinner. braun's is unwieldy bc it's round in shape so in the end might take up more suitcase room. Also, the panasonic cleaning cartridge is smaller and not alcohol-based. you do have to add tap water to the panasonic. the braun uses alcohol which evaporates over time once you pop the lid open, regardless of whether or not you use it. Update: Have used now for 1 month. Still loving it. Can now comment on the cleaning feature. Does a very good job of cleaning =) Quite economical too! I was able to get refills from Amazon 3-pack for $8.88. I clean once every 3 days, 1 cartridge supposed to last ~ 1.5 months, but i can see stretching it even longer duration. That 3-pack i just got should last me 6 months, just buck and half per month, well worth the convenience and quality of cleansing. braun cleaner is bulky, more expensive, will run you at least $10 for a 2-pack and you can't really stretch the life too much b/c alcohol based, will evaporate over time whether you use it or not, once it's been opened. A whole 3-pack of panasonic is smaller in size than a single braun cartridge. braun's cleaner had lemony scent which is nice, panasonic has no scent, just like out of the box. does take up to 3x longer to clean than braun, but for me that has turned out to be more academic rather than practical issue. i usually run the cleaner after a shave not before i need to use. just push the button and leave; so i don't care if it takes 1 or 3 hours since i won't be coming back to use the shaver until the next day anyway. hope that helps.

  116. I purchased the ES8077S shaver six months ago, after I gave up on getting replacement batteries for my ES8033--both are linear-motor powered--that gave me four-years of satisfying use. The old shaver had NiCad batteries, and had dropped to half a shave per charge. The ES8077S has NiMH batteries that easily give me 10 days of use on a single charge. The charge indicator (low, med, high) has been quite accurate for me, as opposed to several other reviewer's comments. I don't think the shave is any better with the new \\"Vortex\\" shape and the new 30 degree angle blades, but it's the best I can get with an electric. The 13,000/minute cutting speed is essential to the shave, I think, since I tried the cheaper model that runs at 10,000/minute (my wife gave it to me as a present, not appreciating the difference), and I returned it per the warranty. I even got my money back--after 8 weeks. The major distinction of the Panasonic is its waterproof case. Shaving with cream and warm water gets the closest shave, but it's about as must work as shaving with a blade--and just as messy. I can get shaving burn that way, but sometimes it is useful. I can usually shave dry in about 90 seconds. I tried shaving in the shower, but you can't shave and wash at the same time, since you must hold the razor as well as the washcloth, and you need a good mirror on the wall of the shower or in your hand. I still like the idea of a waterproof razor. Braun's razors are not guaranteed waterproof, but their cleaning system requires immersion. I never used the Braun system, but the Panasonic \\"HydraClean\\" system is very, very impressive from the technological standpoint. It uses water-based soap--unlike the Braun--whose solution contains alcohol. Since I am allergic to alcohol, I prefer this system. It runs like a dishwasher, filling twice from the tank, pumping the aqueous solution in and out without any spillage. It is noisy, but it's in the bathroom and the door can be closed.The drying phase can continue for up to three hours, but this does not use the razor's motor, as suggested by some reviewers. You can choose to charge the battery with each use, using a single button on the left, which cycles through the choices, indicated on the three green LEDs on the right. You get better life out of the battery if you drain it to \\"low\\", so I don't usually use the \\"charge\\" option. The first left button push removes the \\"charge\\" LED option, and the process begins in about 15 seconds. I clean my razor about every three days, but the cartridges last longer if you wash out the inside of the razor first. A red LED below the green LEDs glows when the cartridge is defunct. I bought 12 of them for $15 with the razor, and I have only used two so far. It makes the razor \\"smell better\\" and I think it cuts best after cleaning. I don't know if it tends to dull the razor as some reviewers have claimed. I like to shave with a safety razor every week or two, but I like shaving dry after a shower--although Braun suggests that you shave BEFORE you wash! Electric shave lotion and after-shave lotion contain alcohol, so I don't use them. It's easier to shave dry with your shirt on--or even your tie! I didn't think I would use the cleaning system, but after trying it, I am impressed. I think it has more technology than the razor!

I didn't find the razor noise to be obnoxious. Insofar as the cleaning cycle is concerned--yes, it's loud, but only for the first 15 minutes or so of the cycle (after that, the remainder of the 3 hour cleaning cycle is relatively quiet or even silent). <br /> <br />The self-cleaning unit does a perfect job of eliminating all the hair and residue from the razor (another reason I purchased this model...I really wanted the convenience). <br /> <br />Now, for the warning. <br /> <br />Although I used the automatic cleaning unit exclusively from the time I bought the shaver in March, when I went on vacation in September it was time to switch to a \\"manual\\" cleaning mode. In this instance, because it's not practical to take the cleaner/charger unit on the road, the instructions tell you to essentially rinse the screen and cutter components under a tap with soap, and then manually dry them. Which I did. Just like the directions told me. After all, the instructions point out that the unit is \\"waterproof.\\" <br /> <br />The next time I activated the shaver, it ran for a few seconds and then quit. I stared at it in front of the mirror in bewilderment (which did not help). I turned the unit upside down, and water trickled from it. I flicked it several times. More water came out. And then the unit starting running normally again. <br /> <br />So much for being \\"waterproof.\\" <br /> <br />I just decided from that point on to keep the shaver away from water, and everything was fine. But come March (after owning the shaver a little less than a year), the motor starting changing speeds randomly, slowing down, and pulling hair rather than cutting it. And there was a thin film of lubricant extruding from inside the motor housing. <br /> <br />In another forum, I read about one other owner who had a horror story of returning the ES8077 to Panasonic, and waiting six weeks for a response. I'm happy to report that my situation turned out more favorably--I sent the shaver portion back via UPS with my original receipt (with a note that pointed out that the shaver was never waterproof). In about two weeks, they sent back a *complete* unit to me, including a new charger/base unit, which I never even expected, all for free. <br /> <br />So here's the advice I'd pass along, which I followed myself: when you buy the shaver, test it by going through a manual cleaning procedure under the faucet. Find out if it seems to trap water in the housing, or otherwise ceases to run properly after having been exposed to water. In my case, there seems to be no trapped water escaping from the housing when I turn it upside down. And the shaver runs perfectly after rinsing it. Because this shaver *is* waterproof. <br /> <br />So buy it. But test it. That's my advice.

I would break it down like this: Pros: *wet/dry capability (wet is strongly recommended, and is the main reason to consider a Panasonic in the first place). Close shave (though not as close as other Panasonic models) *Linear motor (shaver runs at a constant speed until the battery runs dead, unlike non-Linear models which get gradually slower with each use. *Battery power indicator. *Cleaning/charging base. *Lithium-ion batteries. *Close shave. Cons: *Shave is not as close as lesser-expensive Panasonics. *Cleaning cartridges for the base unit are hard to find in stores. *Pivoting head (not a necessary feature in my opinion). *Not an OUTSTANDING shave. I had this shaver for almost two years (daily use), at which point it developed a water leak, no doubt due to the added complexity of the pivoting head, and the motor shorted out. My previous Panasonic shavers lasted 4-5 years, so I expected nothing less than 4 years out of this one. Ultimately, rather than shipping it to Panasonic for repair/replacement (at my cost), I purchased a cheaper Panasonic two-blade shaver. I STRONGLY recommend the Panasonic wet/dry shavers, but not this model. Now if Panasonic would just put a Linear motor in one of their single or double-blade models...

  223. before i get into my review of this shaver, i am compelled to give a little background of my skin type and the problems ive had with shaving. i'm a 25 yr old white guy with medium beard thickness. i have sensitive skin that is prone to bumps and ingrown hairs if i shave too close. i have tried many aftershave products and none has completely eliminated the problem. for years, ive been using the gillette mach III razor(and before that the sensor excel), but due to the sensitivity of my skin, i have been limited to shaving in the downward direction. this method has never given me a very close shave. a few months ago, i got fed up with having a 5:00 shadow at noon and decided to try an electric shaver. <br /> <br />i figured it would be worth it to buy the top of the line shaver. most of them have what i consider \\"luxury\\" features, such as the cleaning base unit, travel plugs, and cases. these are nice, but not very important to me. i want a razor that gives a nice shave all over (face and neck), doesn't hurt during the process, and doesn't leave my skin red and dried out when im done. i have also read some complaints of a shaver and/or the base being loud, but while some are louder than others, none are going to wake up the neighbors. when reading my review of the 3 shavers i tried, keep in mind that a shaver that has these three qualities makes me happier than one with a cool base and a travel kit. <br /> <br />anyway, lately Braun has been flooding the airwaves with ads for the new Braun Activator, so i figured i should give it a shot. at first, i was very happy with the Activator. it has a strong motor and when i applied it to my 2 day beard growth, it mowed right through. i did have trouble around my neck, as the Braun just wouldn't cut the rather long hairs there. i went over the area quite a few times, which left my neck red and with a couple of nicks. i ended up having to use a regular razor just to clean up the spots along my neck that it wouldn't cut. i also noticed that after a few days, it left my face chaffed. it had a nice trimmer on it and for those who care, the cleaning base was actually kind of nice and it did indeed make the shaver feel just like new after each shave, but i would have gladly sacrificed that for a better neck area shave. <br /> <br />so i tried Braun's chief competitor, Norelco. again, i went for the high end model, the SoftTouch. my first impression of the SoftTouch was of its rather weak motor. it just didn't feel very powerful to me, but to my surprise it shaved a teensy bit closer than the Activator and it was much more successful around my neck. after a few shaves with it, however, i noticed some problems. first, if i skipped shaving for a day, i had to use a blade because the SoftTouch just couldn't do it efficiently. i'd spend 10 minutes shaving with it and i'd still have hairs that it just hadn't cut. no good. secondly, it pulled. i don't feel i was moving it over my skin too quickly, but even after just one days growth, i felt the little blades tugging on some of the hairs. i actually started shaving slower out of fear of that very uncomfortable tug. it too seemed to have some trouble around my neck. while better than the Activator, it actually cut the hair on my neck, however it also left some nicks. the trimmer is equally weak and i had to work at it to get a nice even line on my sideburns. also, for some reason, it isn't very good at using it to get the stray whisker. sometimes, it just doesn't cut that pesky hair even though you are holding it right up to it. <br /> <br />so after using it for a month (they ask you to try it 21 days), i sent it back. i did not buy the one with the cleaning unit, but it wasn't hard to clean at all. and i liked how it told you when it was dirty and when it needed new blades (though, obviously i didn't have it long enough to see them in action). <br /> <br />lo and behold, i was perturbed by the results my little test. then i remembered that i had owned a Panasonic shaver back in high school. it was very simple by today's standards, but i never had a problem with it. so i figured i should check out what Panasonic had to offer. <br /> <br />i bought the ES8077S Vortex with high hopes. at $129 on amazon, it was cheaper than the other two i had already bought and returned. i have only owned it for a week now, but i already know that this is the shaver for me. so let me rave about it a little bit. <br /> <br />the Vortex, like the Activator, has a powerful motor. it cut through my beard without any problem and left me with a softer, smoother shave than either of the others. it shaves my face nice and smooth with absolutely no pulling. and also important, i don't feel dry and chaffed afterwards. in fact, i can apply aftershave, right after using the shaver and only experience a very minimum sting, less eventhan a regular blade. i can't say the same about the other two shavers. the Braun, in particular, really left my face burning when i applied aftershave. <br /> <br />around my neck area, the Vortex isn't perfect. i have a hard time getting some of the hairs, but it does a much better job than the Activator and even after going over it a few times, the Vortex doesn't nick or leave my skin raw. and if i flip up the trimmer, i can easily clean up what it misses, again with no pain or irritation. the trimmer is powerful and has no difficulty with stray hairs. it is also safe to drag it across your skin without worrying about nicks or cuts. <br /> <br />so the Vortex is far and away the best of the 3 shavers in my opinion and this is without even using one of its key features. the Vortex is a wet/dry shaver, whereas the Activator and SoftTouch can not be used wet. i am getting the closest, most comfortable shave with it and i haven't even used it with water yet. this means that i can get an even closer shave if i use it with gel/shaving cream. <br /><br />it comes with a cleaning base, which works nicely. if i had to offer one criticism of the Vortex, i guess i'd say it is not as quiet as the SoftTouch, but with its more powerful motor, i would gladly sacrifice the quietness for a good shave and no pulling. <br /> <br />all in all, if you are going to spend over $100 on an electric shaver, check out the Panasonic line first. i think it blows away all the other guys, which is suprising. i hope you found this helpful. sorry for writing this much, but i wish i had a review like this when i was shopping for shavers.

  254. This shaver's dry shaving is good. But its wet shaving is very problematic. Though the manufacturer claims it's wet/dry, the blade and screen is not well designed for wet work. When using foam in shaving, the skin becomes more sensative and tender, which requires the blade to be sharp as a real razor. Panasonic certainly cannot meet this. Though they claim the inner blade is the sharpest 30 degree blade up to date, the more useful two outer blades are still 90 degree. The holes on the screen are also too big for wet shaving, though they are OK for dry work. Because of these design flaws, after applying foam in a wet shaving, more sensitive skin goes into the holes and is scanned by blunt blades. The result is terrible-- the shaver peeled off a very thin layer from my side cheek skin and caused a large area of irritation. Now, my cheeks are full of scars. <br />This Panasonic one is not ready to be a good wet shaving product.

  265. Pros: Long battery life, easy to clean by rinsing with water. Cons: Idiotic handle and pivot design, takes a very long time to shave, difficult to shave several areas, can tear up the skin, no lock button. This shaver is not as good as most people here seem to think. Coming from several Brauns, this is a step down. The handle and pivot design are extremely inappropriate to an electric shaver. An electric shaver is NOT a razor, and shouldn't have the handle of one - this handle makes it hard to maneuver around the face. The side-to-side pivoting of the head is not very useful. In an electric shaver, fore-and-aft pivoting is what contributes to a quick, close shave, and this shaver lacks it. To get a close shave with this thing, you need to go back and forth 5-10 times over the same area from different directions. It's even worse when shaving wet - I would recommend staying with dry shaving. Areas under the chin, around the adam's apple, and at the back of the jaw are extremely difficult to shave with this shaver. If you lather up, you will likely bleed in these areas if trying to get a close shave. Again, stay with dry shaving - it's easier on the skin. The charging / cleaning base is a little gimmicky and noisy, but I do like the dry-only feature - dries the shaver after rinsing. And that is a good feature - cleaning is very easy. Pop off the foil, rinse under water, and that's it! I only use the cleaning cartridge once a week. I have used this shaver for over a month, and the battery life is excellent. You can go longer than a week before recharging. And long battery life comes in handy with this shaver, because it takes a long time to shave - up to 10 minutes versus 3-4 minutes with my old Braun. I plan on continuing to use this shaver for a couple of years, but I'm going back to Braun when it's time to replace it.

  283. Reader's Digest version: great electric shaver, with as near to a good blade shave as I've found.<br />Background: I'm a 31 yr old white man with moderate beard hair that grows in a mildly complex pattern. I've had significant difficulty with post-shave irritation and occasional ingrown hairs. I've been using a DE (dual edge) razor and a silver tip brush with shave soap or cream lathered in a Moss scuttle for several years now, starting with hot soak, followed by shave oil, soap/cream, with/across/against the grain, then alum block finished with good aftershave. This is the benchmark against which I compare any other shaving methods.<br />I purchased this razor through Amazon when it was Panasonic's premier shaver, and thus have several years and blade changes with this one. I've also had Norelcos and Brauns (though admittedly never their top models).<br />A good wet, blade shave takes about 20 minutes start to finish. Sometimes one does not have the luxury of taking over half an hour for bathing and dressing. It is in this circumstance that I current utilize this razor.<br />If one has but 2-3 minutes, this razor will allow a visually acceptable dry shave whose palpable closeness is less underwhelming than other dry shaves I've experienced (but still suboptimal). However, if one's schedule allows 5 minutes addition to the shower for a quick wet shave (using a quality cream such as e-Shave), the results to the hand and post-shave facial skin narrowly lag behind full blade-and-badger wet shave, with a major difference only being apparent in the amount of time before stubble becomes apparent to the touch and the eye: a close traditional shave typically results in palpable stubble by 24 hours, followed by visual stubble at 36-48 hours, whereas a shave with this razor lasts but 8-12 hours by touch, followed at 20-24 hours by the appearance of a beard shadow.<br />All in all, this a quality addition to my shaving toolbox, and comes closer than any other electric razor to the closeness of a good traditional shave in far less time, and with no more irritation than that from a careful blade shave.
